<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver, British Columbia</a>, Canada, from February 12 to February 28, 2010. A total of 2,632 athletes representing 82 <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> participated in these Games.<sup id="cite_ref-numbers_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-numbers-1">[1]</a></sup> Overall, 86 events in 15 <a href="/wiki/Olympic_sports" title="Olympic sports">disciplines</a> were contested; 46 events were open to men, 38 to women and 2 were mixed pairs.<sup id="cite_ref-Events_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Events-2">[2]</a></sup> Two disciplines were open only to men: <a href="/wiki/Nordic_combined_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Nordic combined at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Nordic combined</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ski_jumping_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Ski jumping at the 2010 Winter Olympics">ski jumping</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Figure skating at the 2010 Winter Olympics">figure skating</a> was the only sport in which men and women competed together in teams.<sup id="cite_ref-Events_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Events-2">[2]</a></sup> Two new events were introduced: men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_skiing_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Freestyle skiing at the 2010 Winter Olympics">ski cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cross_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cross-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Medals were won by 450 individual athletes from 26&nbsp;countries; 19 of those countries won at least one gold. <a href="/wiki/Canada_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Canada at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Canada</a> won its first gold medal at an Olympic Games it hosted, having failed to do so at both the <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1988_Winter_Olympics" title="1988 Winter Olympics">1988 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>. Canada finished first in gold medal wins and became the first host nation since <a href="/wiki/Norway_at_the_1952_Winter_Olympics" title="Norway at the 1952 Winter Olympics">Norway in 1952</a> to lead the gold medal count, with 14.<sup id="cite_ref-clinch_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clinch-4">[4]</a></sup> Canada also broke the record for the most golds won at a single Winter Olympics, which was previously 13, set by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_at_the_1976_Winter_Olympics" title="Soviet Union at the 1976 Winter Olympics">Soviet Union in 1976</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Norway at the 2002 Winter Olympics">Norway in 2002</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RecordGolds_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RecordGolds-5">[5]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="United States at the 2010 Winter Olympics">United States</a> placed first in total medalsits second time doing so in a Winter Gamesand set a record for most medals won at a single Winter Olympics, with 37, breaking the previous record of 36, set by <a href="/wiki/Germany_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Germany at the 2002 Winter Olympics">Germany in 2002</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-clinch_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clinch-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_individual" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics  Men's individual">men's individual</a> event in <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics">biathlon</a>, two silver medals were awarded for a second-place tie. No bronze medal was awarded for that event.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Athletes from <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Slovakia at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Slovakia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anastasiya_Kuzmina" title="Anastasiya Kuzmina">Anastasiya Kuzmina</a>  <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics">biathlon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics  Women's sprint">women's sprint</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Belarus_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Belarus at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Belarus</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aleksei_Grishin" title="Aleksei Grishin">Aleksei Grishin</a>  freestyle skiing, <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_skiing_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_aerials" title="Freestyle skiing at the 2010 Winter Olympics  Men's aerials">men's aerials</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> won the first Winter Olympic gold medals for their nations. <a href="/wiki/Norway_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Norway at the 2010 Winter Olympics">Norwegian</a> cross-country skier <a href="/wiki/Marit_Bj%C3%B8rgen" title="Marit Bjørgen">Marit Bjørgen</a> was the most successful athlete, winning three gold, one silver and one bronze medal, and became the ninth Winter Olympian to win five medals at one edition of the Games. Chinese short-track speed skater <a href="/wiki/Wang_Meng_(speed_skater)" title="Wang Meng (speed skater)">Wang Meng</a> also won three gold medals.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medal_leaders">Medal leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_2010_Winter_Olympics_medal_winners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Medal leaders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg/220px-BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg/330px-BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg/440px-BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="644"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BjoergenSprintGold2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The medal winners in the <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Cross-country skiing at the 2010 Winter Olympics  Women's sprint">women's sprint</a> in cross-country skiing, from left to right: <a href="/wiki/Justyna_Kowalczyk" title="Justyna Kowalczyk">Justyna Kowalczyk</a> (left) <a href="/wiki/Marit_Bj%C3%B8rgen" title="Marit Bjørgen">Marit Bjørgen</a> (center) and <a href="/wiki/Petra_Majdi%C4%8D" title="Petra Majdic">Petra Majdic</a> (right).</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg/220px-2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg/330px-2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg/440px-2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1257" data-file-height="1677"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_Medals_in_500_metres_short_track.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The medal winners in the <a href="/wiki/Short_track_speed_skating_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_500_metres" title="Short track speed skating at the 2010 Winter Olympics  Women's 500 metres">women's 500 metres</a> in short track speed skating, from left to right: <a href="/wiki/Marianne_St-Gelais" title="Marianne St-Gelais">Marianne St-Gelais</a> (left) <a href="/wiki/Wang_Meng_(speed_skater)" title="Wang Meng (speed skater)">Wang Meng</a> (center) and <a href="/wiki/Arianna_Fontana" title="Arianna Fontana">Arianna Fontana</a> (right).</div></div></div>
<p>Athletes that won at least two gold medals or at least three total medals are listed below.
